Interdiction Due to Debt – Imam vs Sahibayn
Dispute on whether a debtor is interdicted at creditors' request

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on interdiction due to debt and distinguish between the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits interdiction of a debtor to protect creditors, though Imam Abu Hanifa originally rejected it.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether a person overwhelmed by debt can be interdicted at the creditors' request. Imam Abu Hanifa opposed it, arguing it strips legal capacity, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allowed it to safeguard creditors' rights. The later scholars adopted the Sahibayn's view, making it the operative ruling for fatwa. We will examine the reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the overall Hanafi position
Identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling on interdiction due to debt. According to the Sahibayn, it is permissible; the fatwa is on their view.
Imam Abu Hanifa's view is not the operative one.
2
Identify the intra-madhhab disagreement
Recognize that Abu Hanifa held that interdiction degrades human dignity and likens the person to animals, causing great harm, so it is not permitted. The Sahibayn disagreed.
This is a legitimate scholarly difference within the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's evidence and reasoning
The Sahibayn's position is based on the need to protect creditors from harm. They consider that insolvency can be adjudged, and the qadi can interdict to prevent further loss.
The text cites al-Nawadir: the issue rests on the concept of iflas (insolvency).
4
Examine the practical implementation
The interdiction applies only to property existing at the time of the order; later acquisitions (e.g., earnings, inheritance) are not affected. The debtor retains capacity to transact with new assets. The debtor must be informed of the interdiction.
This limits the scope of interdiction, as per al-Inaya and al-Tatarikhaniyya.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its significance
The author states 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' — the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view. This is the position a mufti should give.
This shows that later Hanafi scholars weighed the harm to creditors as more severe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : قوله : (ودين) وإن طلب غرماؤه يعني لا يحجر عليه بسبب الدين ولو طلب غرماؤه الحجر عليه وهذا عند الإمام لأن في الحجر عليه إهدار أهليته وإلحاقه بالبهائم وذلك ضرر عظيم فلا يجوز وعندهما يجوز عليه بسبب الدين وعلى قولهما الفتوى ؛ كذا . قاضيخان من باب الحيطان. وفي الكافي : والكلام في الحجر بالدين في موضعين: أحدهما أن يركبه دين مستغرق لماله أو يزيد على أمواله وطلب الغرماء من القاضي أن يحجر فيحجر عليه ويمنع من البيع والتصرف والإقرار حتى لا يضر بالغرماء، وفي النوادر: مسألة الحجر بسبب الدين بناء على مسألة القضاء بالإفلاس والإفلاس عندهما يتحقق في حال حياته فيمكن القاضي القضاء بالإفلاس. وفي العناية وإذا قضى بالحجر بسبب الدين يختص بالمال الموجود في الحال دون ما يحدث من الكسب أو غيره حتى لو تصرف في الحادث نفذ، وإذا صح الحجر بسبب الدين صار حال هذا المحجور عليه كحال مريض عليه ديون الصحة، وكل تصرف يؤدي إلى إبطال حق الغرماء فالحجر يؤثر فيه. وفي التتارخانية يشترط علم المحجور عليه حتى يصير محجوراً عليه. وفي النوادر : وإذا حبس الرجل في الدين ينبغي للقاضي أن يشهد أنه قد حجر عليه في ماله حتى يقضي ديونه التي حبس فيها.
He (the author) said: His statement: 'And debt' meaning if his creditors request it, he is not interdicted due to debt even if his creditors request interdiction upon him. This is according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] because in interdiction upon him there is degradation of his legal capacity and likening him to beasts, which is great harm, so it is not permitted. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is permitted due to debt, and the fatwa is on their view. Thus in Qadikhan from the chapter of caution. And in al-Kafi: The discussion of interdiction due to debt is in two places: one that he has debt overwhelming his wealth or exceeding his assets, and the creditors ask the judge to interdict, so he interdicts him and prevents him from selling, transacting, and confessing so that he does not harm the creditors. In al-Nawadir: The issue of interdiction due to debt is based on the issue of judgment of insolvency, and insolvency according to them is realized during his life, so the judge can judge insolvency. In al-Inaya: If he is interdicted due to debt, it is specific to the property existing at the moment, not to what he later acquires or other, so that if he disposes of what he later acquires, it is valid. And if interdiction due to debt is established, his state becomes like that of a sick person who has debts from health, and every disposition that leads to voiding the right of the creditors, the interdiction affects it. In al-Tatarikhaniyya: Knowledge of the interdicted person is a condition for him to become interdicted. In al-Nawadir: If a man is imprisoned for debt, the judge should testify that he has interdicted him over his property until he pays the debts for which he was imprisoned.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding whether a person overwhelmed by debt can be interdicted at the creditors' request. Abu Hanifa denies it, arguing it strips the person of legal capacity and demeans him, causing great harm. The Sahibayn allow it to protect the creditors' rights. The author notes that the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view, making this the operative ruling. The passage then quotes various sources explaining the details: the interdiction applies only to existing assets, not later acquisitions; it limits dispositions that harm creditors; and the interdicted debtor must be notified. This shows the practical implementation of the Sahibayn's position.

Key Terms
إفلاس (iflas): Insolvency; a state where a person's debts exceed his assets.
حجر بالدين (hajr bi al-dayn): Interdiction imposed due to overwhelming debt to protect creditors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position, what happens to a person who is interdicted due to debt?
A) He is prevented from all transactions, including those with new property.
B) He is only prevented from transactions that harm creditors, and his later acquisitions are not affected.
C) He loses all legal capacity like a minor.
D) He is imprisoned but not interdicted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ultimately adopted the view of the Sahibayn that a debtor can be interdicted to protect creditors, though the interdiction only affects existing assets, not later acquisitions.

Definition and Signs of Puberty in Hanafi Fiqh
Definition and evidentiary ruling on legal markers of puberty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of bulugh, list the signs of puberty for males and females, and identify the default age limits when signs are absent.

Core Idea
Puberty ends minority: marked by physical signs (wet dream, emission, pregnancy) or default ages (18 male, 17 female).

Understanding the legal onset of puberty (bulugh) is crucial because it ends the period of minority (sughr) and brings full legal responsibility (taklif). The Hanafi school defines it through specific physical signs and, in their absence, through maximum age defaults. This lesson presents the definition, the evidence from hadith, and the positions of the early Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Define bulugh linguistically and terminologically
Understand that bulugh linguistically means 'arrival' and terminologically it is the end of minority. This sets the stage for the legal threshold.
The terminology is key to understanding why precise markers are needed.
2
Identify the signs of puberty for males
List the three signs: ihtilam (wet dream), ihbal (impregnation), and inzal (emission). Note that each independently establishes puberty.
The hadith from Ali states 'no orphanhood after puberty' linking wet dream to adulthood.
3
Identify the signs of puberty for females
List the three signs: hayd (menstruation), ihtilam (wet dream), and hami (pregnancy). Menstruation is the most common sign.
The text argues that menstruation usually occurs at childbearing age, making it a reliable indicator.
4
Apply the default age rule when signs are absent
For males: default age is 18 years (or 19 in one narration). For females: default age is 17 years. Understand the reconciliation of the 18 vs. 19 narration.
The reconciliation: '19 years' is interpreted as entering the 19th year, i.e., after completing 18.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is 18 for males and 17 for females (the view of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and a narration from Abu Hanifa). Note that the Shafi'i school agrees with this hadith evidence.
The mufta bihi is the position of the Sahibayn; the alternative narration from Abu Hanifa is not operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في حد البلوغ
البلوغ في الغة الوصول وفي الاصطلاح انتهاء حد الصغر. ولما كان الصغر أحد أسباب الحجر وجب بيان النهاية بهذا الفصل . قال رحمه الله : (بلوغ الغلام بالاحتلام والإحبال والانزال وإلا فحتى يتم له ثمانية عشر سنة الحلمُ بالضم ما يراه النائم، أما الاحتلام فلما روي عن علي بن أبي طالب قال : حفظت من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يتم بعد احتلام ولا قوم إلى الليل رواه أبو داود والحبل والإحبال لا يكون إلا مع الاتزال وأما السن فلما روي عن ابن عمر قال : عرضت على رسول الله يوم أحد وأنا ابن أربع عشرة سنة فلم يجزني. وعرضت عليه الخندق وأنا ابن خمس عشرة سنة فأجازني. فالظاهر أن عدم الإجازة لعدم. يوم البلوغ والإجازة للبلوغ وهذا قول أبي يوسف ومحمد وهو قول الإمام الشافعي ورواية عن أبي حنيفة. وعن الإمام في الغلام تسع عشرة سنة قيل المراد أن يطعن في التاسع عشرة فلا اختلاف بين الروايتين لأنه لا يتم ثمانية عشر سنة وإلا ويطعن في التاسع عشرة، وقيل فيه اختلاف الروايتين حقيقة لأنه ذكر في بعض النسخ حتى يستكمل تسع عشرة سنة. ولما كان الذكر أشرف قدم ما يتعلق به قال رحمه الله: (والجارية بالحيض والاحتلام والحبل وإلا فحتى يتم لها سبع عشرة سنة أما الحيض فلأنه يكون في أوان الحبل عادة فجعل ذلك علامة
Section on the definition of puberty. Puberty (bulugh) linguistically means arrival, and terminologically it means the end of the period of minority. Since minority is one of the causes of interdiction (hajr), it was necessary to explain its endpoint in this section. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (The puberty of a boy is through wet dream, ejaculation, and emission; otherwise, until he completes eighteen years.) Wet dream (ihtilam) is what one sees while sleeping. As for wet dream, it is based on what was narrated from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib: he said, 'I memorized from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): There is no orphanhood after puberty, and no silence until night' – reported by Abu Dawud. Pregnancy and impregnation occur only with emission. As for age, it is based on what was narrated from Ibn 'Umar: he said, 'I was presented to the Messenger of Allah on the day of Uhud while I was fourteen years old, and he did not permit me. I was presented to him at the trench while I was fifteen years old, and he permitted me.' So it appears that the non-permission was due to lack of puberty, and the permission was due to puberty. This is the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and it is the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, and a narration from Abu Hanifa. From the Imam (Abu Hanifa) regarding the boy: nineteen years. It is said that what is meant is that he enters into the nineteenth, so there is no difference between the two narrations because he does not complete eighteen years without entering the nineteenth. And it is said that there is a real difference between the two narrations because in some copies it says 'until he completes nineteen years.' Since the male is more honorable, he began with what pertains to him. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And the girl's puberty is through menstruation, wet dream, and pregnancy; otherwise, until she completes seventeen years. As for menstruation, it is because it usually occurs at the time of pregnancy, so it is made a sign.)
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the legal age of puberty (bulugh) in the Hanafi school, which is important because minority (sughr) is a cause for interdiction (hajr). The text first defines puberty terminologically as the end of minority. The ruling for males: a boy reaches puberty through three physical signs: ihtilam (wet dream), ihbal (impregnating a woman), and inzal (emission of semen). If none of these signs appear, the default age is 18 Hijri years. The evidence for wet dream is a hadith from 'Ali: 'There is no orphanhood after puberty' indicating that after a wet dream, legal responsibility is complete. For age, the hadith of Ibn 'Umar shows that at 14 he was not allowed to fight, but at 15 he was allowed, indicating puberty was attained. This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) and a narration from Abu Hanifa. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa that the age is 19 years, but some reconcile it by saying it means entering the 19th year (i.e., after completing 18 and starting the 19th). For females: puberty is through hayd (menstruation), ihtilam (wet dream), or hami (pregnancy). If none, the default age is 17 years. The evidence for menstruation is its usual occurrence at childbearing age, making it a sign of maturity. The text notes that since the male is more honorable (ashraf), the rulings pertaining to him are presented first.

Key Terms
البلوغ (al-bulūgh): The end of minority, marked by physical signs or reaching a maximum age.
الاحتلام (al-iḥtilām): A wet dream (nocturnal emission), a sign of puberty.
الإحبال (al-iḥbāl): Impregnating a woman, a sign of puberty for males.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default age for female puberty in the Hanafi school when no signs appear?
A) 15 years
B) 17 years
C) 18 years
D) 19 years

Key Takeaway
Puberty in Hanafi fiqh is established by physical signs or, in their absence, by reaching the maximum default ages of 18 for males and 17 for females.

Minimum Ages for Puberty Claim and Fatwa Age
Explains the minimum ages for accepting a claim of puberty and the fatwa age.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum ages for accepting a claim of puberty and the fatwa age according to the Hanafi school, and explain the rationale for the difference.

Core Idea
Minimum claim ages are 12 (boys) and 9 (girls); fatwa age is 15 for both.

This passage clarifies a crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the age at which a child's own claim of puberty is accepted (12 for boys, 9 for girls) versus the default age at which puberty is legally presumed (15 for both). The commentator explains the reasoning behind these thresholds and confirms the relied-upon position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two ages
Locate the minimum ages for accepting a claim of puberty (12 for males, 9 for females) and the age used for fatwa (15 for both). Note that these are different: 12/9 are thresholds for a claim, 15 is the default age for legal rulings.
The passage explicitly states 'Fatwa is given on puberty for both at fifteen years...' and 'the minimum period for him is twelve years and for her nine years.'
2
Understand the rationale for the minimum ages
The commentator explains that women's growth is faster, so the minimum age for girls is lower (9 vs 12). For boys, including a full year covering the four seasons ensures the body matures appropriately. The ages are known through oral transmission and empirical tracking.
This reasoning (talil) is based on physiological observation.
3
Distinguish between acceptance of claim and the actual ruling
The minimum ages (12/9) are only for accepting the child's statement. Once accepted, the child is treated as an adult. However, in the absence of a claim, the general ruling is that puberty is presumed at 15. This prevents premature adult responsibilities without a verified claim.
The claim is accepted because the state of puberty is not externally verifiable; it parallels accepting a woman's word about menstruation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi variant
The fatwa age of 15 is attributed to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Abu Hanifa may have held a different view, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the 15-year default.
The commentator states this is the apparent position needing no further explanation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخمسة عشر سنة وأدنى المدة في حقه اثنتا عشرة سنة وفي حقها تسع سنين فإن راهقاً وقالا قد بلغنا صدقاً وأحكامهما أحكام البالغين . في البلوغ، وأما الحبل فلأنه دليل على الإنزال لأن الولد يخلق من ماء الرجل والمرأة غير أن النساء نشوهن وإدراكهن أسرع فزدنا سنة في حق الغلام لاشتمالها على الفصول الأربع التي منها ما يوافق المزاج لا محالة فيقوى فيه قال رحمه الله : ويفتي بالبلوغ فيهما بخمسة عشر سنة) عند أبي يوسف ومحمد وهذا ظاهر لا يحتاج إلى الشرح . قال رحمه الله : (وأدنى المدة حقه اثنتا عشرة سنة وفي حقها تسع سنين يعني لو ادعيا البلوغ في هذه المدة تقبل منهما ولا تقبل فيما دون ذلك لأن الظاهر تكذيبه قال في العناية : ثم قيل إنما يعتبر قول بالبلوغ إذا بلغ اثنتي عشرة سنة فأكثر وقد أشار إليه بقوله «أدنى المدة» وهذه المدة مذكورة في النهاية وغيرها ولا يعرف إلا سماعاً أو بالتتبع . قال رحمه الله : (فإن راهقاً وقالا قد بلغنا صدقاً وأحكامهما أحكام (البالغين يقال رهق من كذا أي دنا منه، وصبي مراهق دنا من البلوغ لأنه أمر لا يوقف عليه إلا من جهتهما فيقبل فيه قولهما كما يقبل قول المرأة في الحيض والله تعالى أعلم .
By fifteen years, and the minimum period for him is twelve years and for her nine years. If they are on the verge of puberty and say 'We have reached puberty,' they are believed and their rulings are the rulings of adults. Regarding puberty, as for pregnancy, it is evidence of ejaculation because the child is created from the fluid of the man and the woman, except that women's growth and perception are faster, so we added a year for the boy because it includes the four seasons, among which is what suits the temperament inevitably, so it strengthens him. He (the author) said: 'Fatwa is given on puberty for both at fifteen years according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and this is apparent and needs no explanation.' He said: 'The minimum period for him is twelve years and for her nine years,' meaning if they claim puberty in this period, it is accepted from them, and not accepted below that because the apparent is that they are lying. It is said in al-Inayah: 'Then it was said that the statement of puberty is only considered when one reaches twelve years or more,' and he indicated it by his saying 'the minimum period,' and this period is mentioned in al-Nihayah and others, and it is only known through hearing or by investigation. He said: 'If they are on the verge of puberty and say we have reached puberty, they are believed and their rulings are the rulings of adults.' It is said: 'rahiqa min kadha' i.e., he came close to it, and a boy is murahiq when close to puberty, because it is a matter that is only known from them, so their statement is accepted as the statement of a woman regarding menstruation. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding the minimum age for accepting a claim of puberty and the actual age of puberty according to the fatwa. The author first states the ruling: fatwa is given on puberty at fifteen years for both males and females, based on the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. However, the minimum age for accepting a claim of puberty is twelve years for a boy and nine years for a girl. If a child who has reached these ages claims to have attained puberty, the claim is accepted and they are treated as adults. Below these ages, the claim is not accepted because the outward circumstance indicates falsehood. The commentator explains the reasoning: the minimum ages are derived from observation and are known through oral transmission or empirical tracking. The term 'murahiq' refers to one who has approached puberty, and since the state of puberty is only known from the individual themselves, their word is accepted, analogous to a woman's statement about her menstruation. The passage clarifies that the actual age of puberty for legal purposes (fatwa) is fifteen, but the lower ages are thresholds for accepting their claim.

Key Terms
البلوغ (al-bulugh): The legal age of maturity, after which a person is responsible for religious obligations.
راهق (rahiq): One who is on the verge of puberty, close to attaining it.
أدنى المدة (adna al-mudda): The minimum period from birth after which a claim of puberty is accepted: 12 years for males, 9 for females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At what age does the Hanafi school give fatwa on puberty according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?
A) 12 years for boys, 9 years for girls
B) 15 years for both
C) 18 years for boys, 15 for girls
D) 17 years for both

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the age at which a child's claim of puberty is accepted (12/9) and the default age for legal rulings (15).

8 min
The Nature of Permission to a Slave: Isqat vs Tawkil
Defending the Hanafi view that permission is isqat, not tawkil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that permission to a slave is an isqat (dropping of right) and distinguish it from the Shafi'i/Zufar view that it is tawkil, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of each view.

Core Idea
A slave's trade permission is an irrevocable isqat, not a delegable agency—it cannot be restricted by the master.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a master permits his slave to engage in trade, the nature of that permission determines its scope. Is it a delegation of authority (tawkil) that can be limited, or is it the dropping of the master's right (isqat) that is inherently general? This passage from al-Bahr al-Rai'iq resolves the question by defending the Hanafi view that it is an isqat, leading to the rule that such permission cannot be restricted by time, place, or type of trade. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying rulings on the authorized slave's transactions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the nature of permission
Identify that the Hanafi school defines permission (idhn) as an isqat (dropping of the master's right) and fakk al-hajr (removal of restriction). This definition is the foundation for the ruling that it cannot be restricted.
The text explicitly says 'it is neither restricted nor specialized'.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i and Zufar consider permission as tawkil (agency). Therefore, they allow restrictions by time, place, or type, as one can limit an agent.
Their view treats the slave as an agent, not as one acting with his own capacity.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The Hanafi school provides analogical reasoning: just as isqat in divorce and manumission cannot be restricted, so too does permission to a slave—because the master's right is dropped irrevocably. Also, the slave acts with his own capacity, not as a representative.
The text draws an explicit parallel with divorce and manumission (qiyas jaliy).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to opposing arguments
The text anticipates objections: if permission were a complete isqat, donations (gifts) by the slave would be valid, which they are not. The Hanafi response is that the isqat is partial—only in commercial matters, not donations. Also, the slave's incapacity to own by gift is due to his status, not the nature of permission.
The objection about gifts is rebutted by noting that permission is not a dropping with respect to non-commercial acts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical result: according to Hanafis, a master's restriction (e.g., 'trade only in land') is invalid, and the slave may trade in land and sea. According to Shafi'i/Zufar, such a restriction is valid and the slave must comply.
This difference directly affects the validity of the slave's contracts if he exceeds a restriction.

Source Text

كتاب المأذون بيان أذن العبد، وأما بيان إذن الصبي فعلى سبيل التبعية، ويجوز أن يكون مدار ما ذكر في تفسير المأذون في الشرع على ما هو المقصود بالذات في كتاب المأذون وهو إذن العبد. ولقائل أن يقول : إن أريد إسقاط الحق بجملته وفك الحجر برقبته فهو ممنوع ولو كان كذلك تصح هبته وإقراضه ونحوهما من التبرعات وليس كذلك قطعاً، وإن أراد أنه إسقاط وفك في الجملة فهو مسلم لكن لا يثبت به المدعي إذ لا يلزم منه إسقاط وفك في جميع التصرفات حتى يكون مأذوناً في جميعها. قيل : المراد إسقاط وفك في بعض معين من التصرفات فلا يرد النقض بالتبرعات فلو قال فك الحجر ومنع إسقاط في نوع لكان أولى فتأمل. قال رحمه الله : فلا يتوقف ولا يتخصص) يعني لا يتوقف بزمان ولا مكان ولا يتخصص بنوع من أنواع التجارة عندنا لما ذكرنا من تفسيره وقال الإمام الشافعي وزفر : هو عبارة عن توكيل وإنابة فينفذ عندهما ويتخصص، وعندهما يتصرف بأهلية نفسه وحق المولى قد أسقطه والساقط لا يعود كما إذا رضي المستأجران يؤجر عبده من شخص بعينه دون غيره والإسقاط لا يقبل التقييد دون غيره كالطلاق والعتاق ولو أسلم البائع المبيع إلى المشتري قبل نقد الثمن على أن يتصرف فيه نوعاً من التصرف دون غيره فإنه لا يعتبر تقييده لأنه إسقاط لحقه فلا يقبل التقييد بخلاف إذن القاضي فإنه بمنزلة الوكيل ؛ ذكره قاضيخان في فتاواه كذا ذكره الشارح. وفي المحيط : يجوز الإذن للصبي العاقل في التجارة من الأب والقاضي ولا يجوز تخصيصه بنوع دون نوع كالعبد لا يقال لو كان إسقاطاً لماء ملكه بهبة لأنا نقول ليس بإسقاط في حق ما لم يوجد فيكون النهي امتناعاً فيما لم يوجد لا يقال هو وليس بأهل لحكم الملك فكيف يكون أهلاً لنفس التصرف والسبب غير مشروع لذاته فإذا لم يترتب عليه حكمه لا يكون مشروعاً كطلاق الصبي لأنا نقول : حكمه ملك اليد وهو أهل لذلك كالمكاتب قال في العناية وصحح المصنف كونه إسقاطاً عندنا بقوله ولهذا لا يقبل التأقيت ثم قال : فإن قيل قوله فك الحجر وإسقاط الحق مذكور في حيز التعريف فكيف جاز الاستدلال عليه؟ وأجيب بوجهين: أحدهما أن حكمه الشرعي هو تعريفه فكان الاستدلال عليه ليس بالاستدلال وإنما هو الصحيح للنقل بما يدل على أنه عندنا تعرف بذلك كما أشرنا إليه. الثاني من حيث كونه حكماً لا من حيث كونه تعريفاً. قال في المحيط : فيبيع من المولى ويشتري منه ويطالبه بإيفاء الثمن على وجه لو امتنع يحبس. ولو قال أذنت لك في الخياطة أو الصباغة أو في عمل آخر فهو مأذون في جميع الأوقات ما لم يحجر عليه، ولو قال اتجر في البر ولا تتجر في البحر لا يصح نهيه ولقائل أن يقول : إن أريد بقوله فلا تخصيص بنوع دون نوع أنه لا يتخصص بذلك. أطلقه ولم يقيده بنوع فهو يسلم لكن لا طائل لأن ما نحن صورة التقيد وإن أريد أنه لا يتخصص بنوع دون نوع وإن قيده بذلك فهو ممنوع ، كيف وهذا يتوقف تمامه على أول المسألة هو أن يكن الإذن في نوع من التصرف وهو يجدي . بل لحكمه
Book of the Authorized Slave: Explanation of the permission of the slave, and as for the explanation of the permission of the minor, it is by way of subordination. It is possible that the basis of what is mentioned in the definition of the authorized slave in the Shariah is what is intended by itself in the Book of the Authorized Slave, and that is the permission of the slave. Someone may say: If what is meant is the complete dropping of the right and the removal of restriction entirely, it is forbidden; and if it were so, his gift, loan, and similar donations would be valid, and that is certainly not the case. And if he intended that it is a dropping and removal in general, that is conceded, but the claim is not established by it because it does not necessitate dropping and removal in all transactions such that he becomes authorized in all of them. It was said: The intended meaning is dropping and removal in some specific transactions, so the objection by donations does not apply. So if he said 'removing the restriction and preventing dropping in a type', it would be better, so consider. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'So it is neither restricted nor specialized', meaning it is not restricted by time or place, nor is it specialized by a type of trade according to us, due to what we mentioned from its definition. Imam al-Shafi'i and Zufar said: It is an expression of delegation and deputyship, so according to them it is effective and specialized. According to them, he acts with his own capacity, and the master's right has been dropped, and what is dropped does not return, like when the lessor is satisfied that he rents his slave to a specific person and not others, and dropping does not accept restriction without others, like divorce and manumission. If the seller delivers the sold item to the buyer before paying the price on condition that he disposes of it in a certain type of disposal and not others, then its restriction is not considered because it is dropping his right, so it does not accept restriction, unlike the permission of the judge, for it is in the position of an agent. Qadi Khan mentioned this in his Fatawa, as the commentator mentioned. In al-Muhit: Permission for a discerning minor in trade from the father and the judge is permissible, and it is not permissible to specialize it by a type without another, like the slave. It cannot be said: If it were a dropping, he would not own it by gift, for we say: It is not a dropping with respect to what does not exist, so the prohibition is prevention regarding what does not exist. It cannot be said: He is not qualified for the ruling of ownership, so how can he be qualified for the act itself? And the cause is not legislated for itself, so if its ruling does not result, it is not legislated, like the divorce of a minor. For we say: Its ruling is ownership of possession, and he is qualified for that, like the mukatib. He said in al-Inayah: The author confirmed that it is a dropping according to us by his statement: 'And for this reason it does not accept temporal limitation.' Then he said: If it is said: His statement 'removing restriction and dropping of right' is mentioned in the context of definition, so how is it permissible to use it as evidence? It is answered in two ways: First, that its legal ruling is its definition, so using it as evidence is not actually evidence; rather it is correct for transmission that indicates that according to us it is defined by that, as we indicated. Second, from the perspective of it being a ruling, not from the perspective of it being a definition. He said in al-Muhit: He sells from the master and buys from him, and demands payment of the price in such a way that if he refuses, he is imprisoned. If he said: 'I have permitted you in tailoring, or dyeing, or another work,' he is authorized in all times as long as he is not placed under restriction. And if he said: 'Trade in the land and do not trade in the sea,' his prohibition is not valid. And someone may say: If what is meant by his statement 'no specialization by type without another' is that it is not specialized by that, he released it and did not restrict it by type, that is conceded but has no benefit because we are in a situation of restriction. If what is meant is that it is not specialized by a type without another even if he restricts it by that, it is forbidden. How? And this depends on the completion of the first issue: that the permission in a type of disposal is sufficient? But for its ruling...
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the nature of permission (إذن) given to a slave to engage in trade. The author clarifies that according to the Hanafi school, this permission is an 'isqat' (dropping of the master's right) and 'fakk al-hajr' (removal of restriction), not a 'tawkil' (agency). The key consequence is that because it is an isqat, it cannot be restricted by time, place, or type of trade. The passage begins by defending this definition against objections, then contrasts it with the views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Zufar who consider it a delegation (tawkil). The Hanafi school argues that isqat is irrevocable and cannot be conditioned, analogous to divorce and manumission. Examples are given: if the owner says 'trade in land but not in sea,' the restriction is invalid. The text also discusses that if the owner permits the slave in a specific craft like tailoring, that still constitutes general permission in all times and places. The dispute includes responses to potential objections, such as the validity of gifts by an authorized slave (they are not valid, which proves it is not a complete isqat). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that permission is an isqat, and thus general and unrestricted.

Key Terms
إسقاط (isqat): The dropping or relinquishment of a right; here, the master drops his right to control the slave's commercial activities.
توكيل (tawkil): Agency or delegation, where the slave acts as the master's representative.
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave who has been given permission by his master to engage in trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a master tells his slave 'I permit you to trade in land but not in sea,' what is the ruling?
A) The slave may only trade in land; the restriction is valid.
B) The slave may trade in both land and sea; the restriction is invalid.
C) The slave may only trade in sea; the restriction reverses the permission.
D) The permission becomes void because it is conditional.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school views permission to a slave as an isqat (dropping of right), making it inherently general and unrestricted, unlike agency which can be limited.

Pledge by the Permitted Slave (Ma'dhun)
Rulings on a ma'dhun slave giving and receiving pledges (rahn).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a ma'dhun's pledge transactions and identify when other creditors can prevent such a pledge.

Core Idea
A ma'dhun slave can pledge and accept pledges as trade supplements, but preferential payment to one creditor can be blocked by others.

This lesson examines the capacity of a ma'dhun (permitted slave) to engage in pledges (rahn). As a key figure in Hanafi commercial law, the ma'dhun is authorized by his master to trade, and the question arises whether he can also give and take pledges as part of his business. The classical Hanafi text clarifies that rahn is a supplement of trade, so it falls within the slave's authority. However, specific conditions and limitations apply, especially when debts are involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The ma'dhun gives and takes pledges. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) because it is a supplement of trade.
The act is permitted despite the slave's status because it is ancillary to the trade for which he is authorized.
2
Examine the dalil (proof)
The proof is that rahn involves payment (ifa') and receipt (istifa'), which are core elements of trade. Thus it is subsumed under the trade permission.
The text states: 'because they are from the supplements of trade, because they are payment and receipt.'
3
Analyze the al-Asl case
If the slave has a debt and pledges an item placed with the master, and it perishes, the debt remains and the loss is from the slave's wealth. The master cannot act as agent to collect from his own slave.
This illustrates that the master is not a suitable pledgee when the slave has debt, because collection is compromised.
4
Consider creditors' rights
If the ma'dhun wants to pledge to one creditor as settlement, other creditors can prevent it because the pledge is effectively a payment (ifa' hukman) that prioritizes that creditor.
This prevents unfair preferential treatment among creditors.
5
Apply the absolute scope of the ruling
The author's statement covers all situations: with or without debt, whether the slave's assets are fully encumbered, and whether the pledge is to the master or to others. Specific conditions apply: if no debt, pledging to master is valid; if debt exists, pledging to creditors is suspended (mawquf).
The 'absolute' statement means the general validity is universal, but the details vary based on the presence of debt and the pledgee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (يرهن ويسترهن لأنهما من توابع التجارة لأنهما إيفاء واستيفاء ويتقرر ذلك بالهلاك. قال في الأصل : إذا كان على العبد دین فرهن به رهناً ووضعاه على مولاه وهلك في يده لم يبطل دين الغريم وهلك الرهن من مال العبد لأن المولى لا يصلح وكيلاً بقبض الدين من عبده فكذا لا يصلح عبده، ولو لحق المأذون دين فأراد أن يرهن عبداً من بعض الغرماء فللباقين المنع لأن الرهن إيفاء حكماً .اهـ. وأطلق قوله «يرهن» فشمل ما إذا كان عليه دين أو لا، كان مستغرقاً أو لا رهن عند المولى أو عند بعض الغرماء. أما إذا لم يكن لا عليه دين يصح إن برهن من المولى، وكذا لو لم يكن عليه دين لأنه إذا لم يصلح أن يكون عدلاً لا يصلح أن يكون مرتهناً، فلو رهن من بعض الغرماء يتوقف كما ذكر في الأصل.
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): "He gives a pledge and takes a pledge because both are from the supplements of trade, because they are payment and receipt, and that is established by destruction." He said in al-Asl: If the slave has a debt and pledges a pledge in lieu thereof, and they place it with his master and it perishes in his hand, the creditor's debt is not voided, and the pledge perishes from the slave's wealth because the master is not suitable as agent to collect debt from his slave, so likewise his slave is not suitable. If the ma'dhun incurs a debt and wants to pledge a slave from some creditors, the others may prevent him because the pledge is a payment in effect. End. And he (author) made his statement 'he gives a pledge' absolute, including whether he has a debt or not, whether it is comprehensive or not, a pledge with the master or with some creditors. As for when he has no debt, it is valid if he pledges from the master; likewise if he has no debt because if he is not suitable as a surety, he is not suitable as a pledgee. If he pledges from some creditors, it is suspended as mentioned in al-Asl.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the capacity of a ma'dhun (permitted slave) to engage in pledges (rahn). The matn states he can give and take pledges because they are ancillary to trade (payment and receipt). The commentary from al-Asl (Imam Muhammad's work) explains a specific case: if the slave has a debt and pledges an item placed with the master, and it perishes, the debt remains and the loss is from the slave's wealth. The master cannot act as agent to collect from his own slave. If the slave wants to pledge to some creditors, other creditors can prevent him because it effectively pays them preferentially. The commentary then elaborates: the absolute statement covers all cases—with or without debt, whether the slave's assets are fully encumbered or not, and whether the pledge is to the master or to others. If the slave has no debt, pledging to the master is valid; if to others, it is suspended (needs permission?). The logic: if the slave cannot be a surety (being owned), he cannot be a pledgee.

Key Terms
الرهن (ar-rahn): A pledge or collateral given as security for a debt.
الإيفاء (al-ifa'): Payment or fulfillment of a debt.
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade.
مستغرقاً (mustaghriqan): Fully encumbered; when the slave's assets are completely taken up by debts.
يتوقف (yatawaqquf): It is suspended; the transaction is pending further condition or permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens if a ma'dhun with debt pledges an item to his master and it perishes in the master's hand?
A) The debt is voided and the master bears the loss.
B) The debt remains and the slave bears the loss.
C) The debt is reduced by the value of the pledge.
D) The master is liable for the pledge.

Key Takeaway
A ma'dhun's pledge transactions are valid as trade supplements, but preferential payment to one creditor can be blocked by others.

Effect of Tadbir and Istilad on the Authorized Female Slave
Explains tadbir and istilad effects on authorized female slave and master's guarantee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether tadbir revokes the authorization of a female slave, and identify when the master becomes liable to guarantee her value to creditors.

Core Idea
Tadbir does not end a female slave's authorization; both tadbir and istilad make the master liable to creditors for her value.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two key rulings regarding the authorized female slave (al-ma'dhun). First, the master's act of tadbir (declaring her free after his death) does not automatically revoke her authorization to trade. Second, both tadbir and istilad (becoming umm walad) trigger a guarantee liability on the master towards the creditors, because these acts prevent the sale of the slave which would have satisfied their debts. The text also discusses the creditor's option to either claim from the master or from the slave's own acquisitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their legal effects
Tadbir and istilad both create rights to freedom for the female slave, but they have different implications for her current status. Tadbir grants freedom in the future, while istilad makes her an umm walad free upon the master's death. The key question is whether these acts affect her ongoing authorization to trade.
Authorization (idhn) is a permission to engage in trade, which lifts the master's right of interdiction (hajr).
2
Determine the ruling on tadbir
The text explicitly states 'لا بالتدبير' meaning the authorized female slave does not become interdicted by tadbir. The reasoning: there is no conflict between tadbir (future freedom right) and authorization (lifting of current interdiction). Custom does not treat tadbir as a form of interdiction, and no explicit evidence of hajr exists from tadbir.
This contrasts with explicit revocation of authorization (like the analogy of food offered then explicitly forbidden).
3
Determine the ruling on the master's guarantee
The master guarantees the value of the slave for the creditors for both tadbir and istilad. The rationale is that by performing these acts, the master has made the slave unsaleable (since a mudabbara or umm walad cannot be sold), thus preventing creditors from satisfying their claims through sale. The guarantee is to compensate the creditors for this loss.
The guarantee is conditional: creditors may choose to hold the master liable or pursue the slave's own earnings.
4
Analyze the creditor's option and intra-madhhab details
Quoting al-Muhit, the text explains that if multiple creditors exist, each may choose either to claim the master's guarantee or to seek payment from the slave's acquisitions. Their choices do not affect each other's rights. If only one creditor, choosing one option invalidates the other.
This shows that the master's liability is not automatic but subject to the creditors' election.

Source Text

كتاب المأذون
والاستيلاد لا بالتدبير ويضمن بهما قيمتهما للغرماء وإن أقر بما في يده بعد حجره
يرضى بخروجها واختلاطها بالرجال في المعاملة والتجارة ودليل الحجر كصريحه بخلاف ما لو أذن لأم ولده صريحاً كما تقدم ونظيره إذا قدم لآخر طعاماً ليأكله حل له التناول فإذا نهاه صريحاً حرم عليه التناول لقوة الصريح. قال في المنتقى : رجل وطئ جارية عبده المأذون فجاءت بولد فإنه يأخذها وعليه قيمتها لأن للمولى فيها حق الملك وذلك يكفي لصحة الاستيلاد كالأب إذا وطئ جارية ابنه وادعاه فإن استحقها مستحق أخذها وعقرها وقيمة الولد ولا يرجع المولى بالضرر لأنه ليس بشراء ولكن يرجع بقيمتها على عبده، ولو وطئ جارية عبده المأذون ولا دين عليه فإن استحقت رجع العبد على البائع بالثمن وبقيمة الولد. قال رحمه الله : (لا بالتدبير) يعني المأذون لها لا تصير محجوراً عليها بالتدبير لأن العادة لم تجز بتحصين المدبرة ولم يوجد دليل الحجر فبقيت على ما كانت إذ لا تنافي بين حكمي التدبير والإذن لأن حكم التدبير انعقاد حق الحرية في الحال وحقيقة الحرية في المآل وحكم الإذن فك الحجر وحق الحرية لا يمنع فك الحجر. وفي الجامع الصغير للحسامي : جارية أذن لها مولاها في التجارة فاستدانت أكثر من قيمتها فدبرها المولى فهي مأذونة والمولى ضامن لقيمتها للغرماء، ولو وطئها فجاءت بولد فادعاه حجر عليها ويضمن قيمتها للغرماء ا هـ . قال رحمه الله : ويضمن بهما قيمتهما للغرماء) يعني ضمن المولى بالتدبير والاستيلاد قيمتهما لأنه أتلف بالتدبير والاستيلاد تعلق حق الغرماء لأنه بفعله امتنع بيعها وبالبيع يقضى حقهم. قال في المحيط : فإذا ضمن المولى القيمة لا سبيل لهم على العبد حتى يعتق وإن شاءوا لم يضمنوا المولى القيمة واستسعوا العبد في جميع دينهم عليه دين الثلاثة لكل ألف اختار اثنان ضمان المولى فضمناه ثلثي قيمته واختار الثالث استسعاء العبد في جميع دينه جاز ولا يشارك أحدهما الآخر فيما قبض بخلاف ما إذا كان الغريم واحداً، فإذا اختار أحدهما بطل حقه في الآخر كما تقدم. وظاهر قوله و ضمن أن يضمن القيمة مطلقاً مع أن الضمان يتوقف على اختيار الغرماء فلو زاد إن شاءوا لكان أولى .
أمانة عنده
Chapter of the Authorized Slave. And istilad, not by tadbir, and he guarantees with both their values for the creditors. And if he acknowledges what is in his hand after his interdiction... he is pleased with her going out and mixing with men in transactions and trade. The evidence of interdiction is like its explicit wording. Unlike if he explicitly authorized his umm walad, as previously. Its analogy: if he presented food to another to eat, it is permissible for him to consume; if he then explicitly forbids him, it becomes prohibited for him to consume, due to the strength of the explicit. He said in al-Muntqa: A man had intercourse with the slave of his authorized slave, and she gave birth. He takes her and owes her value, because the master has a right of ownership in her, and that suffices for the validity of istilad, like the father if he has intercourse with his son's slave and claims the child. If a rightful claimant claims her, he takes her, her dowry (?), and the value of the child. The master does not claim compensation, because it is not a purchase, but he recovers her value from his slave. If he had intercourse with the slave of his authorized slave and there is no debt on him, and she is claimed, the slave recovers the price and the value of the child from the seller. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (not by tadbir) meaning the authorized female slave does not become interdicted by tadbir, because custom does not permit protecting the mudabbara, and no evidence of interdiction exists, so she remains as she was, since there is no contradiction between the rulings of tadbir and authorization. For the ruling of tadbir is the establishment of a right to freedom in the present and the reality of freedom in the future, and the ruling of authorization is the lifting of interdiction, and the right to freedom does not prevent the lifting of interdiction. In al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Husami: A female slave whose master authorized her for trade borrowed more than her value; the master then made her mudabbara; she is still authorized, and the master guarantees her value for the creditors. If he had intercourse with her and she gave birth, and he claimed the child, he places her under interdiction and guarantees her value for the creditors. End quote. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: And he guarantees with both their values for the creditors. Meaning the master guarantees their value by tadbir and istilad, because by tadbir and istilad he has caused loss to the creditors by preventing her sale, and by sale their right is fulfilled. He said in al-Muhit: If the master guarantees the value, they have no recourse against the slave until he is freed; and if they wish, they do not make the master guarantee the value and they seek payment from the slave for all their debt. Regarding a debt of three people, each one thousand: two choose the guarantee of the master, so we make him guarantee two-thirds of its value, and the third chooses to seek payment from the slave for all his debt; it is valid, and one does not share with the other in what he has collected, unlike if there is one creditor, for if one chooses, his right in the other is invalidated, as previously. The apparent meaning of his saying 'he guarantees' is that he guarantees the value absolutely, while the guarantee depends on the choice of the creditors; so if he had added 'if they wish' it would be better.
Trust in his possession.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
The passage opens with a statement about the authorized female slave: she is not interdicted by tadbir (posthumous manumission). The master guarantees her value with both actions—tadbir and istilad (bearing a child)—to the creditors. The text explains that the evidence for hijr (interdiction) is as clear as explicit wording. In contrast, if the master explicitly authorized his umm walad (mother of his child) to trade, that would be different, as explicit wording is stronger. An analogy is given: if someone offers food to another and then explicitly forbids it, the food becomes prohibited. Then a quote from al-Muntqa discusses a case where a man has intercourse with the slave of his authorized slave, resulting in a child. The master takes the slave but must pay her value because he has ownership interest. If the slave is claimed by a rightful owner, the claimant takes the slave, the master pays her dowry (?) and the value of the child, and then the master can recover from his slave. If there is no debt on the slave, the slave recovers from the seller the price and the child's value. Then the text returns to the explanation: 'la bil-tadbir' means the authorized female slave does not become interdicted by tadbir because custom does not resort to protecting the mudabbara, and there is no evidence of hijr. There is no contradiction between tadbir and authorization because tadbir establishes a right to freedom in the future while authorization lifts hijr; the right to freedom does not prevent the lifting of hijr. A quote from al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Husami: if a female slave is authorized for trade, borrows more than her value, then her master makes her mudabbara, she remains authorized, and the master guarantees her value to creditors. If the master has intercourse with her and claims the child, he places her under interdiction and guarantees her value to creditors. Then the text explains 'wa yadmanu bihima qimatahuma lil-ghurama' meaning the master guarantees the value of both (the mudabbara and the one who bears a child) because by doing tadbir or istilad he has caused a loss to the creditors by preventing the sale of the slave, through which their rights could be fulfilled. Quoting al-Muhit: if the master guarantees the value, creditors have no recourse against the slave until he is freed; if they wish, they can not take the guarantee from the master and instead seek the entire debt from the slave. An example: if three people have a debt of 1000 each against the slave, and two choose to take the guarantee from the master, they take two-thirds of the value, and the third chooses to pursue the slave for his entire debt, it is valid; they do not share what they collected. If there is only one creditor, his choice invalidates the other option. The text then notes that the expression 'yadmanu' seems to imply absolute guarantee, but it is conditional on the creditors' choice.

Key Terms
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave whom the master has authorized to engage in trade
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration that a slave will be free upon the master's death
استيلاد (istilad): The act of a master fathering a child on his female slave, making her an umm walad

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does tadbir not interdict the authorized female slave?
A) Because tadbir is a verbal act that cannot affect trade authorization.
B) Because there is no contradiction between the right to freedom (tadbir) and the lifting of interdiction (authorization).
C) Because the master must explicitly revoke authorization, which tadbir does not constitute.
D) Because custom requires that the slave be explicitly forbidden from trading.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir does not revoke the authorization of a female slave, but both tadbir and istilad make the master liable to creditors for her value, subject to the creditors' choice.

The Authorized Slave's Acknowledgment After Interdiction: The Imam vs. Sahibayn
Explaining the validity of the authorized slave's acknowledgment after interdiction, with ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) on the validity of the authorized slave's acknowledgment after interdiction, explain the proofs of each, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa upholds the slave's acknowledgment after hijr based on istihsan; the Sahibayn reject it by qiyas.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the legal capacity of an authorized slave who has been placed under interdiction (hajr). The central question: can his acknowledgment (iqrar) of a debt or specific property still be effective? The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two distinguished students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, provides a clear example of the Hanafi method of balancing analogy (qiyas) with juristic preference (istihsan). By understanding this dispute, you will grasp how Hanafi jurists weight competing proofs and derive practical rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the default ruling
The slave was originally authorized (ma'dhun) to trade; after interdiction his capacity is restricted. The issue: is his acknowledgment of a debt or specific property in his hand valid?
The 'hand' refers to physical possession of trade earnings.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and their qiyas
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the acknowledgment is invalid. Their proof: the authorization that validated it is removed by hijr, and the slave's hand over his earnings is no longer legally considered.
They analogize to cases where the master takes the property or the slave acquires after hijr.
3
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his istihsan
Imam Abu Hanifa says the acknowledgment is valid. His proof: the physical hand remains; the condition for its nullification is that the property is surplus to the slave's needs, and the acknowledgment itself proves need.
Istihsan prioritizes the reality of possession over the general analogy.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Imam's view, the acknowledgment creates a binding debt payable from current acquisitions. Under Sahibayn's view, it is ineffective until freedom, and then only if the slave has property.
The difference affects creditors and the master's rights.
5
Note the authority level
The text presents Imam's view as istihsan and Sahibayn's as qiyas. In Hanafi usul, istihsan often overrides qiyas, making Imam's view the preferred position (mufta bihi) in later fatwa.
However, the author does not explicitly declare tarjih.

He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he acknowledges what is in his hand after his interdiction) — it is valid. And this according to Imam, whether he acknowledges that it is a usurped item or acknowledges a debt, so he pays it from it. And the two said: His acknowledgment is not valid, and that is the analogy, because that which validates his acknowledgment is the authorization, and it has been removed by interdiction, and his hand over his earnings is nullified by interdiction because the hand of the interdicted person is not considered. So it becomes as if the master took it from his hand after interdiction before his acknowledgment, or his interdiction is established by sale and he has an overwhelming debt on what is in his hand after interdiction, then he acknowledges after that, or the wealth in his hand was acquired after interdiction by gathering firewood and the like. For this reason, his acknowledgment regarding his person after interdiction is not valid, so that his person is not sold for debt by consensus. And this does not entail that the master may not take what his absent interdicted slave deposits with him, because the master — he takes it there when he does not know that it is the slave's earnings? If he knows that it is his slave's earnings, he may take it. And the face of istihsan is that that which validates the acknowledgment after interdiction is the hand. For this reason, his acknowledgment before interdiction concerning what the master takes is not valid, while the hand remains in reality. And the condition for its nullification by interdiction is that the earnings in his hand are surplus to his need, and his acknowledgment is evidence of his need. Unlike if the master seized it from his hand before acknowledgment, and unlike his acknowledgment after the master sold him to another, because by entering into his ownership it becomes like another entity; and since it is known that exchange of ownership is like exchange of the entity. And unlike if he has an overwhelming debt, because the right of the creditors attaches to what is in his hand, so his acknowledgment to nullify their right is not accepted; they are given priority, like the sick person when he acknowledges. And unlike his person, because it is not in his hand. And in al-Muhit: If he acknowledged after he was interdicted, and he had a thousand in his hand which his master took, then he acknowledged that it was a deposit for so-and-so, then he became free, nothing is binding upon him, because he is interdicted, he acknowledged a specific thing and there is nothing in his hand from the earnings of authorization, so his acknowledgment is not valid. And if he acknowledged that it was a usurped item in his hand, it is binding upon him when he becomes free. And if he did not take the deposit from him, but he had a debt and he paid it, it is binding upon him when he becomes free. And if he is interdicted and has a thousand in his hand, and he acknowledges it to two men: one of them has a debt of a thousand, and the other a deposit of a thousand. It is either that he acknowledges them separately or jointly. In each case, either he acknowledges the debt first or the deposit first. If he acknowledges them separately — by saying 'I owe a thousand dirhams' and then is silent, then says 'this thousand is a deposit for so-and-so' — then according to Imam, the entire thousand is for the creditor, because when he acknowledged the debt first, the creditor's right attached to it and the thousand became occupied by it, so his acknowledgment of the deposit after that entails nullifying his acknowledgment of the debt, so it is not accepted. And according to the two, it is between them. If he acknowledges the deposit first, then the debt, the entire thousand is for the depositor. As for if he acknowledges them jointly — by beginning with the debt, saying 'so-and-so has a debt of a thousand against me, and this thousand is a deposit for so-and-so' — the thousand is between them half and half. If he begins with the deposit then the debt, the entire thousand is for the depositor according to Imam. The explanation of that: if he acknowledges the debt first then the deposit, the statement (bayan) is found and the place is in his ownership, his statement is valid, so the thousand is split between them, and this is a statement concerning a specific item, not an estimate, so it is valid when connected not when separated. If he acknowledges the deposit first then the debt, the statement is found and the thousand is not in his ownership, and the creditor's right does not attach to that thousand. And if they both claim against him and he says 'you both are truthful,' the thousand is between them half and half according to Imam, and according to the two, the acknowledgment is invalid and the slave is taken for the debt after emancipation. And if a man gives a thousand to an interdicted slave, and the master does not take it until the slave consumes a thousand for another man, then consumes a thousand for another man, the thousand is for the master, and the two debts are on his person. If he consumes a thousand, then the thousand is given to him as a gift, then another debt comes upon him, the gift is applied to the first debt, which he consumed, not the second, because the second debt becomes binding on him while he has no earnings. And the author did not specify the person acknowledged for, so it includes the master. And in al-Asl: And if the authorized slave acknowledges to his master — if he acknowledges a debt, his acknowledgment is not valid, whether he can have debt or not. If he acknowledges a specific item in his hand — if he has a debt, his acknowledgment is not valid; if he does not have a debt, his acknowledgment is valid. And in al-Dhakhira: The authorized slave picks up a foundling and it is not known except by his statement; the master says 'you lie, rather it is with me,' the word is of the authorized slave, because it is an acknowledgment against himself. Do you not see that if he acknowledged a specific item in...
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of an authorized slave's acknowledgment (iqrar) after the master has placed him under interdiction (hijr). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the acknowledgment is valid, whether he acknowledges debt or specific property. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is invalid, and they claim this is the analogical reasoning (qiyas): because the authorization that made the acknowledgment valid is now removed by the hijr, and the slave's hand (possession) over his acquisitions is no longer considered. They compare it to cases where the master has taken the property from the slave's possession before the acknowledgment, or if the slave obtained property after hijr through gathering firewood, etc. They also note that the slave's person (raqabah) is not in his possession, so acknowledgment regarding his person is unanimously invalid. However, the author provides the reasoning for Imam Abu Hanifa's view (istihsan): the factor that validates the acknowledgment after hijr is the continued physical possession (yad) of the property. The condition for the invalidity of the hand due to hijr is that the property in his hand is surplus to his needs; but his acknowledgment indicates his need. This is distinguished from cases where the master has taken the property before the acknowledgment, or if the master sold the slave to another (making the property like another entity), or if there is an overwhelming debt that gives creditors a prior right. The text then provides examples from al-Muhit: if the master takes the property before acknowledgment, the acknowledgment is invalid; if it was a deposit (wadi'ah) and the master takes it, the acknowledgment is invalid; if it was a wrongfully taken item (ghasb), it is valid after freedom. Then there is a detailed discussion about acknowledgment to two claimants—one for debt and one for deposit—with different scenarios of whether the acknowledgment is connected or separate, and the positions of the three imams. The gist is that Imam's view gives priority to the debt if acknowledged first, while the Sahibayn split. Then a case of two claimants both claiming the property: if the slave says 'you both are truthful,' the property is split according to Imam, but the Sahibayn say the acknowledgment is invalid and the slave will be pursued for the debt after freedom. Then a discussion about a gift (hiba) to the interdicted slave and how it is applied first to a pre-existing debt. Finally, a quote from al-Asl about the authorized slave's acknowledgment in favor of his master: it is invalid if it is a debt, but valid if it is a specific property in his hand when there is no debt. The passage concludes with a quote from al-Dhakhira about a foundling: if the authorized slave picks up a foundling and the master denies, the slave's word is accepted because it is an acknowledgment against himself.

Key Terms
حجر (hajr): Interdiction placed on the slave by the master, revoking authorization to trade
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a debt or a specific item in one's possession
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference over qiyas based on equity or custom

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the basis for the validity of the authorized slave's acknowledgment after hijr?
A) The master's residual authorization
B) The slave's physical possession (yad)
C) The slave's potential freedom
D) The creditors' consent

Key Takeaway
The dispute over the slave's acknowledgment after hijr illustrates the Hanafi balance between qiyas and istihsan, with Imam's view prevailing due to its consideration of actual need and possession.

Complex Scenarios of the Interdicted Slave's Acknowledgment
Applying the rules of the slave's acknowledgment to multiple claimants, gifts, and debt priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings to multiple-claimant and gift scenarios involving an interdicted slave's acknowledgment, and distinguish between valid and invalid outcomes based on the order and manner of acknowledgment.

Core Idea
The order and manner of an interdicted slave's acknowledgment (separate/joint, debt/deposit) determine the outcome between multiple claimants.

This lesson builds on the previous dispute by exploring the detailed scenarios found in the source text: acknowledgment to multiple claimants, gifts, and debts. You will learn how the order of acknowledgment (debt first or deposit first) and whether it is separate or joint changes the distribution. These nuanced cases demonstrate the practical application of Imam Abu Hanifa's principle that the hand is valid unless proven surplus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key variables
The slave has a thousand in hand and acknowledges to two people: one claims a debt, the other a deposit. The variables: separate vs. joint acknowledgment, and which acknowledgment comes first.
These variables affect the priority of claims.
2
Apply Imam's rule for separate acknowledgment
If acknowledged separately (debt first, then deposit): the entire thousand goes to the creditor. If deposit first, then debt: goes to the depositor.
The first acknowledgment attaches to the property.
3
Apply Imam's rule for joint acknowledgment
If acknowledged jointly starting with debt: split half and half. If starting with deposit: all to depositor.
Joint acknowledgment allows the slave to clarify both claims.
4
Compare with Sahibayn's view
In separate acknowledgment, Sahibayn split between them. In joint, they agree with Imam on half? Actually, the text only gives their view for separate.
The Sahibayn view is that acknowledgment is invalid, but here they accept the slave's statement? Re-read: 'Wa 'indahuma yakunu baynahuma' for separate. So they give half to each, but for joint they are not mentioned. Possibly they invalidate entirely.
5
Apply to gift and debt scenarios
If a gift is given to the slave and he has prior debts, the gift goes to the master. If he consumes a gift then incurs a new debt, the gift is applied to the earlier debt.
Priority: master's claim over the gift, then debts in order of attachment.

He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he acknowledges what is in his hand after his interdiction) — it is valid. And this according to Imam, whether he acknowledges that it is a usurped item or acknowledges a debt, so he pays it from it. And the two said: His acknowledgment is not valid, and that is the analogy, because that which validates his acknowledgment is the authorization, and it has been removed by interdiction, and his hand over his earnings is nullified by interdiction because the hand of the interdicted person is not considered. So it becomes as if the master took it from his hand after interdiction before his acknowledgment, or his interdiction is established by sale and he has an overwhelming debt on what is in his hand after interdiction, then he acknowledges after that, or the wealth in his hand was acquired after interdiction by gathering firewood and the like. For this reason, his acknowledgment regarding his person after interdiction is not valid, so that his person is not sold for debt by consensus. And this does not entail that the master may not take what his absent interdicted slave deposits with him, because the master — he takes it there when he does not know that it is the slave's earnings? If he knows that it is his slave's earnings, he may take it. And the face of istihsan is that that which validates the acknowledgment after interdiction is the hand. For this reason, his acknowledgment before interdiction concerning what the master takes is not valid, while the hand remains in reality. And the condition for its nullification by interdiction is that the earnings in his hand are surplus to his need, and his acknowledgment is evidence of his need. Unlike if the master seized it from his hand before acknowledgment, and unlike his acknowledgment after the master sold him to another, because by entering into his ownership it becomes like another entity; and since it is known that exchange of ownership is like exchange of the entity. And unlike if he has an overwhelming debt, because the right of the creditors attaches to what is in his hand, so his acknowledgment to nullify their right is not accepted; they are given priority, like the sick person when he acknowledges. And unlike his person, because it is not in his hand. And in al-Muhit: If he acknowledged after he was interdicted, and he had a thousand in his hand which his master took, then he acknowledged that it was a deposit for so-and-so, then he became free, nothing is binding upon him, because he is interdicted, he acknowledged a specific thing and there is nothing in his hand from the earnings of authorization, so his acknowledgment is not valid. And if he acknowledged that it was a usurped item in his hand, it is binding upon him when he becomes free. And if he did not take the deposit from him, but he had a debt and he paid it, it is binding upon him when he becomes free. And if he is interdicted and has a thousand in his hand, and he acknowledges it to two men: one of them has a debt of a thousand, and the other a deposit of a thousand. It is either that he acknowledges them separately or jointly. In each case, either he acknowledges the debt first or the deposit first. If he acknowledges them separately — by saying 'I owe a thousand dirhams' and then is silent, then says 'this thousand is a deposit for so-and-so' — then according to Imam, the entire thousand is for the creditor, because when he acknowledged the debt first, the creditor's right attached to it and the thousand became occupied by it, so his acknowledgment of the deposit after that entails nullifying his acknowledgment of the debt, so it is not accepted. And according to the two, it is between them. If he acknowledges the deposit first, then the debt, the entire thousand is for the depositor. As for if he acknowledges them jointly — by beginning with the debt, saying 'so-and-so has a debt of a thousand against me, and this thousand is a deposit for so-and-so' — the thousand is between them half and half. If he begins with the deposit then the debt, the entire thousand is for the depositor according to Imam. The explanation of that: if he acknowledges the debt first then the deposit, the statement (bayan) is found and the place is in his ownership, his statement is valid, so the thousand is split between them, and this is a statement concerning a specific item, not an estimate, so it is valid when connected not when separated. If he acknowledges the deposit first then the debt, the statement is found and the thousand is not in his ownership, and the creditor's right does not attach to that thousand. And if they both claim against him and he says 'you both are truthful,' the thousand is between them half and half according to Imam, and according to the two, the acknowledgment is invalid and the slave is taken for the debt after emancipation. And if a man gives a thousand to an interdicted slave, and the master does not take it until the slave consumes a thousand for another man, then consumes a thousand for another man, the thousand is for the master, and the two debts are on his person. If he consumes a thousand, then the thousand is given to him as a gift, then another debt comes upon him, the gift is applied to the first debt, which he consumed, not the second, because the second debt becomes binding on him while he has no earnings. And the author did not specify the person acknowledged for, so it includes the master. And in al-Asl: And if the authorized slave acknowledges to his master — if he acknowledges a debt, his acknowledgment is not valid, whether he can have debt or not. If he acknowledges a specific item in his hand — if he has a debt, his acknowledgment is not valid; if he does not have a debt, his acknowledgment is valid. And in al-Dhakhira: The authorized slave picks up a foundling and it is not known except by his statement; the master says 'you lie, rather it is with me,' the word is of the authorized slave, because it is an acknowledgment against himself. Do you not see that if he acknowledged a specific item in...
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of an authorized slave's acknowledgment (iqrar) after the master has placed him under interdiction (hijr). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the acknowledgment is valid, whether he acknowledges debt or specific property. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is invalid, and they claim this is the analogical reasoning (qiyas): because the authorization that made the acknowledgment valid is now removed by the hijr, and the slave's hand (possession) over his acquisitions is no longer considered. They compare it to cases where the master has taken the property from the slave's possession before the acknowledgment, or if the slave obtained property after hijr through gathering firewood, etc. They also note that the slave's person (raqabah) is not in his possession, so acknowledgment regarding his person is unanimously invalid. However, the author provides the reasoning for Imam Abu Hanifa's view (istihsan): the factor that validates the acknowledgment after hijr is the continued physical possession (yad) of the property. The condition for the invalidity of the hand due to hijr is that the property in his hand is surplus to his needs; but his acknowledgment indicates his need. This is distinguished from cases where the master has taken the property before the acknowledgment, or if the master sold the slave to another (making the property like another entity), or if there is an overwhelming debt that gives creditors a prior right. The text then provides examples from al-Muhit: if the master takes the property before acknowledgment, the acknowledgment is invalid; if it was a deposit (wadi'ah) and the master takes it, the acknowledgment is invalid; if it was a wrongfully taken item (ghasb), it is valid after freedom. Then there is a detailed discussion about acknowledgment to two claimants—one for debt and one for deposit—with different scenarios of whether the acknowledgment is connected or separate, and the positions of the three imams. The gist is that Imam's view gives priority to the debt if acknowledged first, while the Sahibayn split. Then a case of two claimants both claiming the property: if the slave says 'you both are truthful,' the property is split according to Imam, but the Sahibayn say the acknowledgment is invalid and the slave will be pursued for the debt after freedom. Then a discussion about a gift (hiba) to the interdicted slave and how it is applied first to a pre-existing debt. Finally, a quote from al-Asl about the authorized slave's acknowledgment in favor of his master: it is invalid if it is a debt, but valid if it is a specific property in his hand when there is no debt. The passage concludes with a quote from al-Dhakhira about a foundling: if the authorized slave picks up a foundling and the master denies, the slave's word is accepted because it is an acknowledgment against himself.

Key Terms
إقرار منفصل (iqrar munfasil): Separate acknowledgment: acknowledging one claim, then later acknowledging another claim regarding the same property.
إقرار متصل (iqrar muttasil): Joint acknowledgment: acknowledging both claims in one statement without interruption.
إقرار للغصب (iqrar lil-ghasb): Acknowledgment that a property is usurped (ghasb) — this binds the slave after freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) All to Zayd (depositor)
B) All to 'Amr (creditor)
C) Half and half
D) The acknowledgment is invalid

Key Takeaway
In complex scenarios, the order and connectedness of the slave's acknowledgment determine the priority of claims, highlighting the precision of Hanafi fiqh in protecting rights.
