Ghasb: Only Movables, Not Land – The Hanafi Position
Expansion of a ruling with inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghasb of immovable property, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and identify the exception for waqf land.

Core Idea
Ghasb requires physical movement; land cannot be ghasb legally.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq defines ghasb (usurpation) as an act that only applies to movable property. The author then presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute, with Abu Hanifa and later Abu Yusuf holding that there is no liability for ghasb of land, while Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i hold that there is. The commentary explains the linguistic emphasis and the practical exception for waqf property.

Guided Path
1
1. Grasp the Definition of Ghasb
Read the first part where ghasb is restricted to 'what can be moved and transferred'. Understand that the Hanafi definition requires physical removal of the property from the owner's control.
The author clarifies that 'naql' and 'tahwil' are essentially the same for this purpose.
2
2. Identify the Core Dispute
Locate the sentence 'If he usurped immovable property and it perished...'. The question is whether the usurper (ghasib) is liable to compensate the value.
The dispute is between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf (later view) vs. Muhammad/Zufar/al-Shafi'i.
3
3. Examine the Supporting Evidence
Review the proofs: the Hanafi side argues that ghasb requires movement, which is impossible for land; ejecting the owner is action on the person, not the property. The opposing side cites possession exclusivity, deposit cases, and the hadith about land.
The Hanafi response rejects the deposit analogy and interprets the hadith as moral rather than legal.
4
4. Note the Practical Exception (Waqf)
Observe the note from al-'Ayni: fatwa is given according to Muhammad's view (liability) for waqf land. This is the operative ruling in that specific context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والغصب فيما ينقل ويحول لأنه إزالة يد المالك بإثبات يد وذلك يتصور في المنقول، قيل النقل والتحويل واحد وقيل التحويل النقل من مكان والإثبات في مكان آخر والنقل يشتمل عليه بدون الإثبات في مكان آخر . المقصود بيان تحقق الغصب فيما ينقل ويحول دون غيره لا بيان مجرد تحققه في المنقول فالقصر معتبر في التركيب المذكور وأداة القصر في هذا التركيب وتعريف المسند إليه بلام الجنس يفيد قصر المسند إليه على المسند كما صرحوا به في علم الأدب ويتلوه نحو التوكل على الله والكرم في العرب، والإمام من قريش. قال رحمه الإمام وأبي الله : (فإن غصب عقاراً وهلك في يده لم يضمنه) وهذا عند يوسف. وقال محمد وزفر والشافعي : يضمنه وهو قول أبي يوسف أولاً. وفي العيني : ويفتى بقول محمد في عقار الوقف. ولأن الغصب يتحقق بوصفين بإثبات اليد العادية وإزالة اليد المحقة وذلك يمكنه في العقار لأن إثبات اليدين المتدافعتين على شيء واحد لا يمكن لتعذر اجتماعهما فيه فإذا ثبت اليد العادية للغاصب انتفت اليد المحقة للمالك ضرورة ولهذا يضمن العقار المودع بالجحود والإقرار به لغير المالك وبالرجوع عن الشهادة بعد القضاء ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام من غصب شبراً من أرض طوقه الله أرضين»(1). ولنا القيامة من سبع يوم أن الغاصب تصرف في المغصوب بإثبات يده وإزالة يدا المالك ولا يكون ذلك إلا بالنقل والعقار لا يمكن نقله وأقصى ما يكون فيه إخراج المالك منه وذلك تصرف في المالك لا في العقار فلا الضمان، ومسائل الوديعة على الخلاف على الأصح فلا يلزمه ولئن سلم يوجب
He (the author) said: (And ghasb pertains to what can be moved and transferred, because it is removal of the owner's hand by establishing a hand, and that is conceivable in movables. It is said that 'naql' and 'tahwil' are one, and it is said that 'tahwil' is moving from a place and establishing in another place, while 'naql' includes it without establishing in another place. The purpose is to explain that ghasb occurs in what can be moved and transferred, not in other things, not to explain its mere occurrence in movables, so restriction is considered in the mentioned construction, and the tool of restriction in this construction and defining the subject with the definite article of genus indicates restriction of the subject to the predicate, as they explained in the science of grammar, and like it is the saying 'Trust in Allah' and 'Generosity among Arabs' and 'The Imam from Quraysh'. He (the Imam and Abu Allah) said: (If he usurped immovable property and it perished in his hand, he does not guarantee it.) And this is according to [Abu] Yusuf. And Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i said: He guarantees it, and it was the first opinion of Abu Yusuf. And in al-'Ayni: And fatwa is given according to Muhammad regarding waqf immovable property. Because ghasb occurs with two characteristics: establishing a wrongful hand and removing the rightful hand, and that is possible in immovable property because establishing two opposing hands on one thing is impossible due to the impossibility of their coexistence. So when the wrongful hand of the usurper is established, the rightful hand of the owner is necessarily removed. For this reason, the guarantor of deposited immovable property is liable by denial, by acknowledging it for other than the owner, and by retracting testimony after judgment. And due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever usurps a span of land, Allah will collar him with seven earths on the Day of Resurrection.' As for us, [our proof is] that the usurper acts upon the usurped property by establishing his hand and removing the hand of the owner, and that does not occur except by movement, and immovable property cannot be moved. The utmost that occurs is ejecting the owner from it, and that is action upon the owner, not upon the property, so there is no liability. And cases of deposit are based on the preferred opinion, so it is not necessary [to extend the analogy], and even if it is accepted...
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage defines ghasb as applying specifically to movable property because it requires physically taking possession (either by moving or transferring). The author clarifies linguistic nuances between 'naql' and 'tahwil'. The core dispute is whether ghasb applies to immovable property (land/buildings). Abu Yusuf initially held that it does not, aligning with Abu Hanifa's view, while Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i hold that it does. The Hanafi position is that since land cannot be physically moved, the usurper merely ejects the owner, not taking possession of the land itself. The opposing proof includes: (1) Possession of the usurper necessarily excludes the owner's possession; (2) A trustee of land is liable if he denies or admits for another; (3) The hadith about a span of land. The Hanafi response is that these analogies (deposit) are not accepted (al-khilaf) and that the hadith refers to moral, not legal liability. The text notes that in waqf land, fatwa follows Muhammad's view (liability).

Key Terms
عقار ('iqar): Immovable property such as land and buildings.
يد عادية (yad 'adiyya): Wrongful or usurping hand (possession without right).
يد محقة (yad muhiqqa): Rightful hand (lawful possession).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The usurper is not liable.
B) The usurper is liable, following Muhammad's view.
C) The usurper is liable only if the land is destroyed.
D) The ruling depends on the intention of the usurper.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ghasb only applies to movables; land cannot be ghasb, but for waqf land, fatwa follows Muhammad's view of liability.

Detention of the Usurper When He Claims the Item Perished: Intra-Hanafi Evidence Dispute
Ruling on detention and intra-Hanafi evidence dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on detaining the usurper who claims destruction and explain the evidence dispute between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding whose evidence prevails after the usurper claims return.

Core Idea
The judge detains the usurper on claim of destruction until convinced; after return, Muhammad and Abu Yusuf dispute whose evidence is preferred.

This lesson examines two related issues from Kitab al-Ghasb: the judge's detention of a usurper who claims the item perished, and an intra-Hanafi dispute on evidence when the usurper later claims the item perished after return. The detention ruling protects the owner's right to the specific item, while the evidence dispute shows how different legal principles (impediment vs. liability) affect burden of proof. Understanding these nuances is critical for applying ghasb law correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the detention ruling and its basis
Read the passage to find the rule: the judge detains the usurper until he is convinced that if the item had remained, it would have been produced. Then judgment is given for the replacement (badal). Note the analogy to a debtor claiming insolvency.
The detention has no fixed duration; it is discretionary.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
After establishing the general rule, the text presents a dispute between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding a specific scenario: the usurper claims the item perished after return, and the owner denies. Identify each imam's position and their evidentiary reasoning.
Muhammad: usurper's evidence preferred (establishes return as impediment). Abu Yusuf: owner's evidence preferred (establishes liability).
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: which party bears the burden of proof in court affects the outcome of liability. If the usurper's evidence is accepted, he is not liable; if the owner's evidence prevails, the usurper must pay the badal.
The text does not give a tarjih; both views are recorded as legitimate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب
غصبه وإن ادعى هلاكه حبسه الحاكم حتى يعلم أنه لو بقي لاظهره ثم قضى عليه ببدله. قال رحمه الله : (وإن ادعى هلاكه حبسه الحاكم حتى يعلم أنه لو بقي لاظهره ثم قضى عليه ببدله) لأن حق المالك ثابت في العين فلا يقبل قوله فيه حتى يغلب على ظنه أنه صادق فيما يقول كما إذا ادعى المديون الإفلاس وليس لحبسه حد مقدر بل موكول إلى رأي القاضي كحبس الغريم بالدين ولو ادعى الغاصب الهلاك عند صاحبه بعد الرد وعكس المالك وأقام البينة فبينة الغاصب أولى عند محمد لأنه تثبت الرد وهو عارض والبينة لمن يدعي العوارض وعند أبي يوسف بينة المالك أولى لأنها تثبت الضمان والآخر منكر والبينة للإثبات وأطلق في قوله «حبسه» ومحله ما إذا لم يرض المالك بالقضاء بالقيمة فإن قلت : قال في الذخيرة إن الغاصب إذا عيب المغصوب فالقاضي يقضي بالقيمة من غير تلوم فما وجه قوله؟ قيل في المسألة روايتان، وقيل المذكور في الذخيرة جواب الجواب والمذكور في الكتاب جواب الأصل؛ كذا في العناية.
Book of Usurpation: If he usurps and claims its destruction, the judge detains him until he knows that if it had remained he would have produced it, then he judges against him for its replacement. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And if he claims its destruction, the judge detains him until he knows that if it had remained he would have produced it, then he judges against him for its replacement.' Because the owner's right is established in the specific item, so his statement is not accepted therein until the judge's assumption is that he is truthful in what he says, just as when the debtor claims insolvency. And his detention has no fixed limit but is left to the opinion of the judge, like the detention of a debtor for debt. And if the usurper claims destruction to the owner after return, and the owner denies and produces evidence, the evidence of the usurper takes precedence according to Muhammad because it establishes return, which is an impediment, and evidence is for the one who claims impediments. According to Abu Yusuf, the evidence of the owner takes precedence because it establishes liability, and the other is a denier, and evidence is for establishing. And he spoke generally in his statement 'detains him', and its scope is when the owner does not consent to judgment for the value. If you say: it is said in al-Dhakhira that if the usurper defected the usurped item, the judge judges for the value without delay, so what is the face of his statement? It is said: in the matter there are two narrations, and it is said that what is mentioned in al-Dhakhira is the answer of the answer, and what is mentioned in the book is the answer of the original; as in al-Inayah.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn regarding the usurper's claim that the usurped item perished. The author explains that the judge detains the usurper without a fixed term until it becomes evident that if the item had remained, he would have produced it, then judgment is given for its replacement (badal). The reason given is that the owner's right is tied to the specific item (ayn), so the usurper's statement is not accepted without the judge's strong presumption of truthfulness, analogous to the case of a debtor claiming insolvency. The detention duration is discretionary, like detention for debt. Then a dispute is noted: if the usurper claims the item perished after return and the owner denies, who prevails? According to Muhammad, the usurper's evidence is preferred because it establishes the 'arid (impediment) of return, and evidence is for the one who claims impediments. According to Abu Yusuf, the owner's evidence is preferred because it establishes liability (daman) and the other is a denier. The commentator clarifies that the detention ruling applies only when the owner does not consent to judgment for the value. Finally, a question is answered regarding an apparent contradiction with al-Dhakhira, explaining that there are two narrations or that al-Dhakhira addresses a different aspect.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation: the act of taking another's property wrongfully and forcibly, establishing one's own hand and removing the owner's hand.
بدل (badal): The replacement or compensation for the usurped item, typically its value (qimah) or a similar item (mithl).
عارض (arid): An impediment that prevents liability from attaching. In this context, return of the item is an impediment to the owner's claim for compensation.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence or proof, typically from witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the owner is a denier
B) Because it establishes the return, which is an impediment
C) Because the usurper is the defendant
D) Because the owner's evidence is weak

Key Takeaway
The judge detains a usurper who claims destruction until convinced; after a claimed return, Muhammad and Abu Yusuf differ on whose evidence prevails, reflecting different principles of evidence in Hanafi law.

Understanding the Scope of Ghasb (Usurpation) in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining ghasb as applying only to movable property with linguistic justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ghasb, explain its restriction to movable property, and identify the linguistic tool (qasr) used in the text.

Core Idea
Ghasb only applies to movables—one cannot 'usurp' land by mere occupation in the Hanafi school.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq defines ghasb as applying exclusively to movable property, grounding this in both the nature of usurpation (removing the owner's hand) and a linguistic analysis of the text. We will unpack the reasoning and the grammatical structure that enforces this restriction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Locate the statement 'wa al-ghasb fima yanqalu wa yahwilu' and understand that ghasb is defined as removal of the owner's hand by establishing a hand.
The definition is the core of the passage.
2
Understand the rationale (talil)
The reason only movables can be usurped is because the action of removing the owner's hand and establishing one's own is only conceivable with movable items.
Land and buildings cannot be physically taken in the same sense.
3
Analyse the linguistic qasr
Examine how the Arabic phrasing with the definite article for genus (al-istighraq) restricts ghasb to movables. The commentator compares it to phrases like 'al-imam min Quraysh' to illustrate qasr.
This confirms that ghasb is exclusively for movables.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والغصب فيما ينقل ويحول لأنه إزالة يد المالك بإثبات يد وذلك يتصور في المنقول، قيل النقل والتحويل واحد وقيل التحويل النقل من مكان والإثبات في مكان آخر والنقل يشتمل عليه بدون الإثبات في مكان آخر . المقصود بيان تحقق الغصب فيما ينقل ويحول دون غيره لا بيان مجرد تحققه في المنقول فالقصر معتبر في التركيب المذكور وأداة القصر في هذا التركيب وتعريف المسند إليه بلام الجنس يفيد قصر المسند إليه على المسند كما صرحوا به في علم الأدب ويتلوه نحو التوكل على الله والكرم في العرب، والإمام من قريش.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And usurpation applies to what can be transported and moved, because it is the removal of the owner's hand by establishing a hand, and that is conceivable in movable property.' It is said that transport and moving are the same, and it is said that moving is transporting from a place and establishing in another place, and transport includes it without establishment in another place. The intended meaning is to clarify that usurpation occurs in what can be transported and moved, not in other things, not merely to clarify its occurrence in movable property. So restriction (qasr) is considered in the mentioned construction, and the tool of restriction in this construction and defining the subject with the definite article of the genus indicates restriction of the subject to the predicate, as they have clarified in the science of adab, and it is followed by examples like 'trust in Allah' and 'generosity among Arabs' and 'the Imam is from Quraysh.'
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling clarifying the precise scope of ghasb (usurpation). The author explains the matn statement that usurpation applies only to what can be transported and moved (manqul), because the essence of ghasb is the removal of the owner's hand and the establishment of the usurper's hand, which is only possible in movable property—one cannot physically take possession of land in the same way. The commentator then discusses the semantics of 'naql' and 'tahwil' and emphasizes that the phrasing with al-istighraq (definite article for genus) restricts the subject (ghasb) to the predicate (movable property), a linguistic rule of qasr. The examples 'al-tawakkul 'ala Allah', 'al-karam fi al-'arab', and 'al-imam min Quraysh' illustrate similar restrictive constructions. The key takeaway is that ghasb legally only applies to movable items, not to real estate, establishing a foundational principle for subsequent rulings on liability.

Key Terms
منقول (manqul): Movable property: items that can be transported from one place to another, in contrast to real estate.
عقار ('aqar): Immovable property, such as land and buildings, not subject to ghasb in the sense of physical possession removal.
نقل (naql): Transport: moving an object from one place to another. Some say it includes both moving and placing, while tahwil specifically includes placing elsewhere.
تحويل (tahwil): Moving and establishing: the action of transferring something from one location and fixing it in another.
قصر (qasr): Restriction: a linguistic construction that limits the predicate to the subject or vice versa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason given in the text for why usurpation applies only to movable property?
A) Because movable property is more valuable
B) Because usurpation requires the removal of the owner's hand and establishment of the usurper's hand, which is only possible in movables
C) Because land cannot be stolen
D) Because the hadith only mentions movables

Key Takeaway
Ghasb in Hanafi fiqh is legally defined as the taking of movable property, excluding real estate.
